Song Ziwen Issues Statement on Japan Yesterday 114

Correcting the Malicious Propaganda of a Certain Japanese Official

National News Agency reports: Song Ziwen, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, stated to a reporter from the National News Agency yesterday that he doubts the truthfulness of a report that a certain responsible Japanese official told news reporters that there was a negotiation between China and Japan that was even more important than the Manchurian issue, but he didn't know where the Chinese government actually was or who was in charge. As far as he remembers, Japanese Minister Akira Ariyoshi had just presented his credentials to the National Government a few weeks ago. If the words of the Japanese official mentioned in the newspaper were true, it would be tantamount to disavowing his own minister, which would only confirm what American politician Frederick Moore said last winter: "(Any country that wants to establish treaty relations with Japan, for the sake of safety, should sign two treaties, one with its Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and one with its General Staff)." Furthermore, Premier Wang Jingwei's trip to Hamburg, Europe for medical treatment was enough to cause rumors of a split in the National Government, but Wang has already made a frank statement, and his colleagues are still serving in the government as usual. It is hoped that outsiders will not ignore the facts and lightly believe the rumors. When the League of Nations convenes in the future, Premier Wang will go to Geneva to discuss countermeasures with the Chinese delegation, which will put an end to such slanders. Although the National Government has repeatedly encountered difficulties, such as the invasion of the Northeast and Shanghai, the great flood last autumn, and the worldwide economic depression, which have all had adverse effects, its power is becoming increasingly consolidated. This spring, as soon as the Japanese army withdraws from Shanghai, it will immediately engage in suppressing the communists, because the communist bandits took advantage of the Japanese invasion to commit acts of violence. At one point, the areas occupied in Anhui, Hubei, and Henan provinces reached 30,000 square miles. After six months of arduous suppression by the National Army, they have now been gradually recovered. The organized communist army has been completely defeated. Only sporadic remnants remain north of the Yangtze River, waiting to be eliminated. Military Affairs Committee Chairman Chiang is now moving a large army to Jiangxi to attack the communist party's main nest. As long as there is no more obstruction from the Japanese army, the communist suppression military operations will be completely concluded in the near future. Those engaging in reactionary propaganda claim that local conflicts in Shandong and Sichuan show that the government is gradually losing power and is a sign of its impending collapse. As a result, those who doubt the current situation may be poisoned by propaganda. In fact, these are all specious arguments. I also believe that the government's forbearance is proof of its growing power. When the Shenyang Incident suddenly occurred last September, I predicted that the era of civil war was coming to an end. In the past, if armed conflicts occurred between warlords, the central government would often issue strict orders to move troops to suppress them. Now, the government knows that unifying by force is both difficult and inappropriate, so it wants to implement moral sanctions and solve local disputes with the help of public opinion. At present, outstanding individuals in the country have organized the "Great Alliance to Abolish Civil War," and its power is growing stronger day by day, soon becoming an important force in abolishing the use of force to solve political problems. Therefore, the central government does not want to easily resort to military force, and will reserve its troops to resist foreign aggression and eliminate those who attempt to use violence to disrupt social order. Moreover, the government's adoption of a policy of forbearance has already yielded significant results. This summer's armed conflict in Guangzhou was therefore limited to one area and gradually subsided on its own. The recent dispute in Shandong province has also been stopped, and there is reason to believe that the turmoil in Sichuan can also be pacified without the use of force by the central government. Now that the people deeply hate civil war, the central government, by complying with public opinion, should see its foundation become more consolidated. Even from a negative perspective, the central government, after adopting a policy of forbearance, can save hundreds of millions in military spending, such as those spent on pacifying domestic rebellions in the past, and can also avoid the distraction of communist suppression military operations. Moreover, it can also begin to carry out construction plans. For example, the government, in the most difficult environment, has completed 2,000 kilometers of embankment along the Yangtze River, which can prevent the recurrence of last year's great flood. As for construction, those familiar with current affairs can see that the government's construction program is becoming increasingly substantial, no longer just empty talk, and has already begun to implement it. The plans it has drawn up must be immediately implementable and able to obtain foreign technical and financial assistance. For example, the Ministry of Railways has plans to complete the Guangdong-Hankou, Cangshi, and Longhai railways, and to reorganize existing railways. Other ministries, with the help of experts from the League of Nations, are also currently planning land rent, rural lending, mass education, central health laboratories, agricultural experiment stations, and expanding telegraphs and telephones, building national highways, and improving the silk industry. As for the government's finances, since the plan to change the domestic debt fund was successful, and the implementation of cutting government spending, and the recent rectification of tax policies, despite encountering unprecedented difficulties in the past nine months, such as the seizure of Northeast customs and salt taxes, it can still avoid raising a debt.

Although the painful cuts in government and military spending have indeed caused much suffering and hindered countless necessary advances, it is a remarkable fact that China is one of the few countries that can balance its budget without borrowing, at a time when very few countries in the world can do so. As the Western saying goes, the proof of the pudding is in the eating. Recently, China's credit abroad has gradually increased and is now among the highest in the world. In the London market in the past twelve months, the post-war reconstruction loan of the Republic of China has risen from 61 to 73, the Anglo-German renewal debt has risen from 82 to 96, and the Anglo-French loan has risen from 50 to 75. Even domestically, the prices of domestic debt have gradually risen in recent months. The rise in the prices of government bonds at home and abroad shows the growing confidence of the outside world in it. This can be regarded as a touchstone for whether the government is stable or not. How can the rumors of those engaged in malicious propaganda be relied on as a tool to spy on the government?

Chen Gongbo Talks About the Central Steel Plant 115

Fundraising methods have been decided

The development program has also been planned

Central News Agency reports: The establishment of the Central Steel Plant has been carefully planned by the Ministry of Industry for several months. The Sino-German contract has been largely agreed upon and will be signed soon. The location of the plant is still under study. Although the contents of the plan and the raising of capital have been recorded in various newspapers, most of them are fragmentary and not detailed. Yesterday morning, a reporter from the Central News Agency visited Minister Chen at the National Trademark Bureau by appointment to inquire about everything in detail, which is recorded below:

Signing of the Official Contract: The Sino-German contract has long been agreed upon. All the machinery and equipment required by the plant will be sold by Germany. However, we can send a specialized committee to inspect whether the purchased machines are excellent, and the specialist can compare their prices with those of products from the United Kingdom and the United States in detail to see if they are low. Only after everything is considered satisfactory will they be allowed to be shipped to China, configured, and applied. As for technical personnel, we are still lacking, so we also plan to have Germany select technicians to respond to our invitations and only provide technical assistance. Therefore, in the future, the Central Steel Plant will be a self-operated enterprise that our government must obtain. The date of signing the contract cannot proceed because the location of the plant has not been resolved. However, the German side has urged us many times, so I hope to resolve the location within a month, and then we can sign the contract at the beginning of next month. The Plant Site Is Undecided: The Ideal of Establishing a Steel Plant: The location should of course be an area with both coal and iron ore deposits, to take advantage of the convenience of obtaining raw materials and the low production costs. The Northeast of our country does have this kind of area. If it were in the South, it would lose the meaning of natural distribution, because our country's iron mines are all south of the Yangtze River, while coal mines are all distributed north of the Yangtze River. Therefore, the location of the steel plant is quite a consideration. Some have proposed setting it up in Pukou. The land and water transportation there is convenient, and it can become the hub of north-south industry and commerce in the future. Therefore, purely from an economic point of view, that place should be very suitable. Moreover, the land there is flat, making it easier and more time-saving to build factory buildings. However, if we want to consider the important meaning of national defense, then this place will inevitably be rejected. As for Ma'anshan, although a survey has been done once, it is still not a very safe place. Although the mountain is high, the neighboring peaks are very short. The Ministry of Military Affairs specially sent several military advisors to go by plane to conduct another aerial survey before a decision can be made. Therefore, I hope to be able to resolve this matter before the end of this month. Coal and Iron Raw Materials: The raw materials required by the steel plant are coal and iron. If we can be self-sufficient, the production cost can be reduced. Therefore, the Central Steel Plant will not only set up a steel plant, but will also mine both coal and iron mines. Anhui Province has abundant reserves of these raw materials. What has been decided now is the Lieshan coal mine and the Yihua and Yuhua iron mines. The Lieshan coal mine can yield 25 million tons of coal when mined to a depth of 1,000 feet. Therefore, in addition to supplying our own use, it can also be sold at a price. The pure content of the Yihua and Yuhua iron mines is 60%, which can continue to be mined for 20 years. Therefore, the steel plant has abundant raw materials. Unfortunately, the capital is limited and it is a new venture, so we cannot plan too big. Therefore, we are only using 80 million as the establishment fund, and the daily output of pure steel is only 500 tons, which is for 5% of our country's total consumption. If there is a surplus in the future, we will expand in order. The iron ore rich in the Dabie Mountains can be used for continued development. Establishment Expenses: The total funds for the steel plant are tentatively set at 80 million yuan, with 10 million yuan used for mining the Lieshan coal mine. 70% of the remaining 70 million yuan, i.e., 49 million yuan, will be used for building the plant site and machinery, and 30%, i.e., 21 million yuan, will be used for mining the Yihua and Yuhua iron mines. This is an estimate, and a precise calculation will be announced later.

Fundraising Methods: The above-mentioned equipment cost of 80 million yuan is difficult to raise at once due to the current financial difficulties of the country. Therefore, it has been decided to issue treasury bonds for half of it, i.e., 40 million yuan, which will be the responsibility of the Central Bank as marketable securities. To ensure credit, the Ministry of Finance will designate a portion of the national tax revenue as collateral. I have already discussed this with Minister Song and have received his approval. The remaining 40 million yuan will be borrowed by the Ministry of Industry with the guarantee of the Lieshan coal production. The Lieshan coal production is estimated at 25 million tons. At 10 yuan per ton, it would be worth 250 million yuan. Therefore, this guarantee is also very noteworthy. In this way, the huge sum of 80 million yuan will be shared by the financial and industrial sectors, making it easier to raise and bear.

Construction Date: If the Sino-German contract can be signed as scheduled, the ministry will send specialists to Germany to inspect the machinery so that it can be shipped to China. The round trip will take about two months. Therefore, three months after the signing of the contract, the first batch of machinery can arrive. If the plant site is set in Pukou, it will be easier to build houses on flat ground. Therefore, three months later, the factory building can also have a considerable scale. If it is set in Ma'anshan, the construction of the hillside will require a lot of work and may take a long time.

Discussing Setting Up a Paper Mill: After the reporter finished the interview and left, Lu Feibohong of Zhonghua Book Company, Wang Yunwu of Commercial Press, and others visited Minister Chen to discuss the establishment of a paper mill. However, no concrete decisions have been made, so it has not been announced. After finishing his work yesterday, Minister Chen took the night train back to Nanjing.

Killing More Than 400 Japanese Military Guards

Intercepting More Than 400 Supply Vehicles

All three Japanese supply trains and 15 wooden carts were also burned clean. It is estimated that more than 40 trains and one locomotive were burned in this battle, preventing the Japanese reinforcements from being supplied. Our army took advantage of the opportunity to capture the city of Ning'an on the 16th at dawn, led by Commander Kong Xianrong with more than 10,000 people. Enemy and our casualties were equal. Since the general offensive on August 8, in just 17 days, more than ten counties have been recovered, including Yanji, Hunchun, Helong, Dunhua, Emu, Shulan, Huaxun, Mengjiang, Antu, Tokyo City, and other counties. East of the Songhua River, it can be said that it is completely under the jurisdiction of this army. The army has nine infantry brigades, and there are also four artillery regiments. The military equipment includes two field artillery pieces, more than 40 mortars, four flat-firing guns, more than 30 machine guns, and about 90,000 rifles. It is also said that the Harbin-Suifenhe line of the Chinese Eastern Railway has not yet been opened to traffic. The area from Suifenhe to Mudanjiang Station is under our army's martial law. From Mudanjiang to Hailin Station is the Japanese military's martial law area (but Hailin Station was captured by our army on the 29th of last month). From Hailin to Yanshi Station and Hengdaohezi is also under our army's martial law. From Hengdaohezi to Yimianpo, it is guarded by the bandit Wang Maosheng (i.e., Little Golden Dragon), who was appointed as the commander of the special operations team by Commander-in-Chief Wang, and is responsible for sabotage work. The front line of our army in the Chinese Eastern Railway is already at Gaolingzi, with a brigade stationed there. Our army also has more than 50,000 special operations teams in the area of Tuquan, Kangping, and Faku in Liaobei, which belong to the Zhilu Army headquarters and are now under the command of Cheng Qinglong, commander of the 12th Route, and Deputy Commanders Wu Lingsaxuan and Zhao Xian. The special operations teams in Andong, Fengshan, and Kuandian in Liaodong are under the command of Yang Fuhai, commander of the 11th Route. Commander Wang's headquarters has a guard of 8,000 men, all of whom are hunters, who can fight for the survival of the nation and never leave until death. They often say that attacking the enemy army is easier than hunting beasts, which is really admirable.

The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Nan Gongmao Yarn Shop Warned for Selling Unlicensed Yarn 126

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Nan Gongmao Yarn Shop, located at the Wan Yu Wharf in Nanshi, this city, suddenly received a warning letter from the Iron Blood Elimination Corps the day before yesterday. The owner of the shop, Tang Zhiliang, is the chairman of the Buddhist yarn market. The corps also sent a letter to the reporter of the Xin Sheng News Agency on Wangping Street in this city, asking to distribute the news to various newspapers. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Warning Letter from the Elimination Corps The Iron Blood Elimination Corps sent a letter to the Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday, stating: Our corps recently discovered that Nan Gongmao Yarn Shop at Wan Yu Wharf is selling Japanese yarn, profiting from the country's misfortune. At this time of intense anti-Japanese sentiment, there are still shameless merchants, which is extremely hateful. We are sending a warning letter to the shop, copied below. Please publish it in major newspapers on behalf of our agency to warn against such behavior and prevent others from imitating it. We believe that your agency is a patriotic organization and will definitely help our corps. The letter is enclosed below: Dear Sir, We recently learned from members of our corps that your shop is selling unlicensed sixteen-count Japanese yarn, which has been found along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway. At this time of intense anti-Japanese sentiment, such shameless behavior is extremely heartbreaking. We are ordering you to stop selling it immediately, otherwise you will face unfavorable bombs and bullets. Sincerely, Tang Zhiliang, Nan Gongmao Yarn Shop. Iron Blood Elimination Corps.

Talk from Nan Gongmao Shop After receiving the letter, the reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Mr. Tang Zhiliang, the chairman of the cotton yarn market. Mr. Tang was away from Shanghai on business, so the reporter went to Nan Gongmao Yarn Shop to inquire. According to the spokesperson of the shop, they have cleared out Japanese goods and stopped selling them since June of last year, and have never purchased Japanese goods since January 28th. The Iron Blood Elimination Corps may have made a mistake in their investigation. However, according to an unofficial report from someone in the cotton yarn industry, the shop has sold unlicensed sixteen-count yarn in the past few days, and its price is lower than that of domestic goods, with the normal price being one hundred and forty taels per piece, while the shop only charges one hundred and thirty taels.

Customs Notice on Visa Fees 127

Tang Hai'an, the superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, the commissioner of taxation, issued a joint notice yesterday, which stated: Regarding the joint notice, the number of consular visas issued by the consulates of the Republic of China abroad and the amount of visa fees paid have been announced on August 18, August 22, September 19, October 19, and November 1 of this year. Item (b) in the announcement of August 22 has now been changed by order of the government to: For goods shipped from overseas in November and December of the 21st year of the Republic of China that do not have a consular visa, the consignee shall pay a visa fee of five customs gold units to the customs to reissue the visa, without having to pay ten customs gold units. Item (c) shall still be handled as before. We should comply with this order, and all merchants should be informed. This notice is issued specifically.

A Large Batch of Silver Dollars from the Bank of China and Others Transported to the Northeast 129

For the Use of Supplying Various Branches

According to Guo Yue News Agency, since the establishment of the puppet state under the wings of the Japanese, it has seized our customs duties and postal and telecommunications services. Financially, there has never been a single cash inflow into the Guannei, so all trade in our country is no longer as active as before, and a large batch of silver dollars has not been transported to the Northeast. Recently, the Bank of China and other banks have transported some, which was handed over to Dongshunji on Jixiang Street, Yishunheng on Jiangxi Road, and Er Customs Brokerage in this city for customs clearance, and transported by Butterfield & Swire's Northern Shipping Line to Dalian Yingkou, then transferred to the South Manchuria Railway to Shenchang. The details obtained by reporters from various parties yesterday are recorded as follows:

A Total of Three Batches Transported　　Reporters inquired with the two shipping and customs brokerage firms yesterday and learned that a total of three batches were shipped by the Bank of China and several other banks. The first batch was seventy boxes, the second batch was twenty boxes, and the third batch was shipped out the day before yesterday (the 5th), totaling one hundred and five boxes. Each box contained 5,000 yuan, totaling about one million yuan.

Bei Songsun's Talk　　Subsequently, the reporter telephoned Bei Songsun, the manager of the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China, to inquire. According to his talk, although the branches in the Northeast provinces are under the puppet government, they continue to operate as usual for business and to maintain credit relations. Regarding the so-called large batch of silver dollars transported to the Northeast, according to my knowledge, the amount is only several hundred thousand, and not as much as one million. In short, this matter is purely for business and has no other purpose.

Lin Kanghou's Opinion　　According to Lin Kanghou's opinion from the Banking Association, the transport of silver to the Northeast is not surprising, as the branches of each bank in the Dong Province have to circulate silver to maintain business. Currently, the Dong Province banks are still operating as usual. If the puppet state causes damage and the branches stop operating, the bank depositors should also be refunded in cash.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to the Public Works Department Requesting Maintenance of Puddle Neighborhoods in Eastern Shanghai 135

Allowing Them to Supplement Registration and Build Huts for Residence

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession yesterday, stating: "Respectfully, we have recently received reports from the puddle neighborhoods on various roads in Yangshupu, stating that your department is demolishing all thatched huts in the area that have not been registered, and even extending to registered huts, destroying all pigpens and furniture. They have requested assistance. Upon investigation, it has been found that these puddle neighborhoods are mostly inhabited by famine refugees and laborers who, due to the high cost of rent in the city, have built their own thatched huts for residence, which is a last resort. Since your department has a precedent of allowing registered residents to live in their huts, those who have not registered are merely lacking in formalities. We request that your department allow them to supplement their registration and continue to build and reside in their huts. Registered residents should especially be legally protected to avoid harassment. Your department should also, within the scope of possibility, provide residential protection for poor residents within the concession to ensure equal treatment. This is what our association hopes for."

Chief Justice Zhou Xianjue of the First Special Court Resigns 137

Approved by the Ministry of Judicial Administration

Guo Yunguan Appointed by the Ministry to Take Over the Vacancy

Zhou Xianjue, the Chief Justice of the Shanghai First Special District Court, due to his intention to retire, petitioned the Ministry of Judicial Administration for resignation. Minister Luo approved it, and Guo Yunguan was appointed by the Ministry to take over the vacancy. Chief Justice Zhou received the telegram a few days ago, and even though it was Saturday, he immediately instructed the staff of each department to begin handling the closing matters, so that he could hand over the position as soon as the new Chief Justice arrived in Shanghai. According to reports, Zhou was originally appointed by the Jiangsu Provincial Government in the 16th year of the Republic of China when the National Revolutionary Army recovered Jiangsu, and came with Lu Xingyuan, who was appointed as the Provisional Court Chief Justice. He initially served as a judge in the Criminal Court, then as a Presiding Judge. When the Provisional Court was reorganized into the Shanghai Special District Court and the Procuratorate was established, he was appointed as the first Chief Prosecutor. It was not until January 25th of this year that he succeeded Yang Hua熉 as Chief Justice. However, only three days after taking office, the January 28th Incident suddenly occurred. The court was adjacent to the Zhabei war zone, and the sounds of gunfire were clearly audible. In addition, Japanese planes flying to the northwest to drop bombs passed directly over the court. During this critical period, Zhou led all the judges and staff of the court to work extra hard and remain calm. Therefore, even though the Shanghai war lasted for more than a month, there was no backlog of civil or criminal cases in the court. In cases where the parties involved in the litigation had fled due to the war and their addresses were unknown, preventing the trial from proceeding, he supervised the clearing of the cases as soon as the war stopped, to ensure that no cases were left pending. In peacetime, he was determined to reorganize the court's affairs and eliminate long-standing malpractices, sparing no effort. He truly deserves to be called a conscientious official.

Hu Yigu Does Not Wish to Transfer 138

Submits Resignation to the Ministry

Hu Yigu, the Presiding Judge of the Civil Division of the Jiangsu High Court, has been in his current position since the establishment of the Rental Court of Appeals at the same time as the reorganization of the Provisional Court after the recovery of the Mixed Court. In the past six years, the name of the court has changed twice, and the chief justice has changed four times, but Mr. Hu has never been transferred. Although he was once temporarily assigned by the Ministry to assume the duties of chief justice, he declined due to his modesty. Recently, the Ministry of Justice issued an order to transfer Hu to serve as the Chief Prosecutor of a certain court in Shandong Province, which seemed to be a promotion. However, it is heard that Mr. Hu is determined to retire due to his age and has declined the appointment. As for his duties in the Second Branch of the High Court, he will hand them over as soon as a replacement is found. It is noted that among the judges in the Public Concession since China established courts there, Mr. Hu is the longest-serving.

Ministerial Order for the First Special Court's Accounting to Be Supervised by the Second Branch of the High Court 139

Merger Must Wait Until the New Chief Justice Takes Office

The accounting matters of the First Special District Court have always been supervised by the Chief Justice of the court and are not subject to the control of the Second Branch of the High Court, which is located in the same place. This system has been in place for many years. Last month, the Ministry of Judicial Administration issued instructions to the two branches of the High Court in the city, the Second and Third Branches, to change the original system. All accounting of the District Court should be merged with the accounting of the High Court and supervised by the Chief Justice of the High Court. It is heard that the Second Special Court in the French Concession has followed the ministerial order and reorganized the accounting department, and has already transferred jurisdiction. Since the situation of the First Special Court is the same, it should also comply. Chief Justice Zhou Xianjue has repeatedly consulted with Shen Jiayi, the Chief Justice of the Second Branch of the High Court, regarding the merger procedures. It is heard that the overall situation has been completed and only needs to be implemented on a scheduled basis. Now, Chief Justice Zhou has suddenly resigned and the ministerial order for his dismissal has been approved. Therefore, the merger of the accounting departments of the two courts must be implemented after the new Chief Justice Guo takes office.

Shanghai to Connect Wireless Telephone with the Three Ports of South China 140

A Prelude to Shanghai's Communication with the World

The Zi Lin Daily reports that wireless telephones are being installed between Hong Kong, Macau, and Guangzhou, and it is expected that communication will be possible by February 15th of next year. Local News Two

Large-Scale Scam: Fictitious Bank Set Up 143

Banknotes Issued Freely, No Money Upon Maturity

Meager Interior, Only a Tea Server

Purchase of Gold Leaf Reveals the Truth

Number of Victims Likely Not Small

Yesterday afternoon at 4 PM, two customers suddenly came to a gold leaf workshop at No. 125 Fuyou Road in the South City, intending to use forged banknotes to swindle gold leaf. Someone noticed and handed them over to the Second Precinct of the First District. Upon further investigation, it was discovered that this was one of a large-scale scam. The details are as follows:

Forged Notes Issued Successively: On the 6th of last month, a certain Zhuang suddenly opened a "Ding Yuan Tai Ji Bank" at No. 8, Jingjiang Lane, Tianzhutang Street, Xinbei. He successively issued a large number of forged notes, secretly instructing his accomplices to use them to purchase a large quantity of goods from major merchants. He then secretly sold the goods. The dates on most of the forged notes were listed as the 6th of this month.

Only a Tea Server Inside: Yesterday, when the maturity dates of the notes arrived, various merchants went to the address to redeem them. However, upon arriving at No. 8 Jingjiang Lane, they saw that the so-called Ding Yuan Bank had only a few desks inside. A young man who looked like a tea servant was inside. When asked his name, he said it was Chen Yongda. The merchants told him they were there to redeem the money. Chen replied that they had to wait for the manager to return. Everyone waited until evening, but there was no news.

Tea Server Only There for Two Days: At this point, the merchants realized that it was a fictitious bank issuing forged notes to obtain goods. They detained Chen Yongda and questioned his background. He claimed that he had previously worked as a tea server at the Ancient and Modern Troupe comedy theater in the New World, and was introduced to this bank by a tourist named Wang. He had only been there for two days and knew nothing about the internal affairs. At that time, each defrauded merchant also specially sent people to guard until 7 PM, still no way, Purchasing Gold Leaf Revealed the Truth:

At the same time, at a gold leaf workshop at No. 125 Fuyou Road in the city, two unexpected customers suddenly came to purchase gold leaf worth over 100 yuan. The two produced a Ding Yuan bank note, falsely worth 250 yuan, and asked the workshop to find change. The workshop happened to have no cash, so they asked them to wait. They immediately sent a shop assistant named Chen Renshan from Shaoxing to the address to verify. Chen arrived at the bank and found out the truth. He immediately returned to the workshop and, together with police officer No. 21 from the precinct, brought the two men and the forged note to the Second Precinct of the First District.

Customers Shift Blame: During the preliminary interrogation by the station chief, Chen Renshan complained about the incident and claimed that the two customers were using fraudulent bank notes to swindle goods, requesting a thorough investigation. When questioned, one customer gave his name as Xu Guang　, 36 years old, from Haimen, who operated a lacquer workshop at No. 11 Lafayette Road in the French Concession. The other customer gave his name as Cai Atao, 35 years old, from the same hometown and in the same industry as Xu. Both claimed that they had received the fraudulent bank note from a customer. They were ordered to stay for investigation and verification.

Many Others Likely Defrauded: Upon investigation, the house where the bank was located belonged to the church. Zhuang rented it from the second landlord, Fuyuan Paper Sundries Store, a month ago to set up this scam. To date, there is no lease contract. According to people at Fuyuan Store, they know nothing about Zhuang's background. In total, there have been two households found defrauded, one is the Xingda Silk Shop on Wuxi Road was defrauded of silk worth more than 800 yuan, one is the Wan Lun Silk Shop in Xiangfen Lane, defrauded of silk worth more than 100 yuan, they are have received a useless bank note in return, As for those who have not shown up, according to the bank note numbers they have issued, it is thought there are still many,

Money Stall on Tongzhou Road Robbed Yesterday Morning 144

Robber Exceptionally Ferocious

Captured Twice, Escaped Twice

Finally Arrested Due to Injury

Russian Man Brave to the End

｜Detective Zhu Jiantang Shot and Killed by Robber｜

Yesterday morning at 10:45 AM, a robbery occurred at the money stall on Tongzhou Road, resulting in the shooting and death of a detective. The details are as follows:

Robber Targets Money Stall: There is a money stall in the Tongzhou Road vegetable market, set up by Wu Zhihao from Zhenjiang, dedicated to exchanging money for the morning market, in order to make a small profit. Yesterday morning at 10:45 AM, just as the market was bustling with activity, the stall was suddenly targeted by a robber wearing a blue short-sleeved shirt and pants. The robber held a pistol in his right hand, approached the money stall, and immediately ordered everyone to be quiet. He grabbed the 138.2 yuan in silver dollars on the stall and stuffed it into his pocket, then turned and fled. Wu Zhihao immediately chased after him, shouting "Robber!" People from nearby vegetable stalls, upon hearing the alarm, also helped to chase after him, about six or seven people, the robber saw behind him tightly after, that would flee to Xinji Bang Road,

Russian Man Intervenes: At the corner where Xinji Bang Road turns, there is a Dongxingji copperware shop. At that time, a Russian architect named Ailes was transacting inside. Upon hearing the sound of catching a robber coming from the Tongzhou Road area, he went outside to watch. He saw a short-clothed man running towards him, looking flustered, and someone chasing closely behind him. He knew that the former must be the robber. So he remained calm, and when the robber ran close to him, he stepped forward and grabbed him. Unexpectedly, the robber was very strong and broke free. Ailes grabbed his left hand. The robber, in desperation, quickly pulled out a pistol from his right pocket and fired at Ailes. Ailes immediately released his hand and dodged behind his own car. The robber escaped and ran forward again wildly.

Ferocious Robber Escapes Twice: After running about ten yards, Ailes came out from behind the car and, seeing the situation, quickly chased after him. The robber turned into Zhoujiazui Road, but Ailes still chased closely. The robber panicked and ran into the right lane of Hexin Lane. The lane employed two Chinese police officers, No. 1874 and No. 3322, as gatekeepers. At the same time, a man named Zhu Jiantang, who worked as a detective at the Old Gate Police Station, happened to live in the lane. When the robber ran in, Zhu happened to be carrying his young child out of the gate. Seeing this situation, he knew that something was wrong, so he quickly put his son down on the ground and met the robber head-on, hugging him around the waist. However, the robber managed to break free with both hands. Zhu then grabbed his left hand. The robber quickly pulled out the pistol from his pocket with his right hand, and Zhu also quickly drew his gun from his arms. The robber took the opportunity to fire four shots at Zhu's hands and feet. Zhu felt intense pain, and his left wrist lost strength. Therefore, the robber escaped again and turned back to shoot Zhu in the face. He was shot in the mouth, and the bullet exited from the back. Zhu fell to the ground.

Detective Dies, Robber Captured: At this time, Chinese police officer No. 1874 quickly fired three shots at the robber, all hitting vital spots. The robber also fell to the ground. Ailes also chased into the lane and, seeing the situation, put his right foot on the robber's body, took the pistol, and searched the robber's body for the stolen goods. At the same time, another police officer, No. 3322, also arrived and quickly reported to the police station. When the patrol police arrived, Zhu had already died from his serious injuries. His body was sent to the coroner's office. The robber was sent to the patrol police hospital, to be sent to the court after he recovered from his injuries. Ailes and others went to the police station to report the incident, signed their names, and left. Zhu Jiantang suffered a total of five injuries: one gunshot wound to the left leg, one to the left foot, one to the right wrist, one to the right leg, and one to the mouth. The robber was shot by the police officer in the left leg, left arm, and back, with severe injuries.

Brick and Ash Industry Tooth Tax Still Receiving One Post 147

Ministry of Finance Approves

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on a letter from the Brick and Ash Industry Guild of this city, requested the Ministry of Finance to order the Shanghai Tooth Post Collection Office to waive the separate collection of two posts. It is now learned that the Ministry of Finance has approved the request. The original text states: "To the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Regarding the Shanghai Tooth Tax Collection Office's separate collection of two posts for brick and ash merchants, the Chamber has telegraphed a request for legal rectification. Before the brick and ash industry's business tax is revised, the original amount should still be collected as one case. The Chamber has already sincerely requested the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance to investigate and reply, and the Chamber has been notified of the instructions. According to Consultation No. 1607 of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance reported that the tooth post tax is specifically for those who open businesses with posts, act as agents for buying and selling, and extract commissions. The business tax is levied based on direct business activities. The nature of the two is different, and there is no duplication. As for the Brick and Ash Industry Guild's claim that the Shanghai Tooth Tax Collection Office requires brick and ash merchants to separately collect two posts, the Jiangsu Province's Reorganization of Tooth Tax Regulations, Goods Items, etc., stipulates two types of businesses: brick and tile businesses and lime businesses. The revenue from this tooth tax has long been allocated to educational expenses. It is unclear how the county's brick, tile, and lime businesses have applied for tooth posts over the years and how this year's situation is being handled. This department has no records available." After the Shanghai County Finance Bureau was ordered to investigate and reply, the director of the bureau, Wang Hua, replied, stating, "The Shanghai brick and ash tooth industry has jointly applied for one post since the Republic of China. Later, due to inconsistencies with the regulations for re-determining the tooth tax regulations and the amount of the goods item table, the bureau ordered separate applications. However, the guild repeatedly stated that business was difficult and they could not bear the increased burden, requesting that the old method be followed." The old method of joint application was approved during the tenure of former County Magistrate Lu, and in July of the 18th year, Instruction No. 1340 of the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office stated, "It is understood that brick and ash are related, and it is claimed that business has been sluggish recently. It is tentatively approved to temporarily allow joint application for one post to show consideration." Two original telegrams were re-examined due to competition from concrete bricks and cement, and business is far from what it used to be. The claim that brick and ash are the same item with the same nature is compared to the fish drying industry not separating fish, crabs, and shrimp and only collecting one post. It is not without reason. Since the brick and ash industry post has already been approved by the Education Funding Management Office to jointly apply for one post, and at a time when the brick and ash business is declining, it seems appropriate to continue to handle it as before to show consideration. The Ministry of Finance will be notified.

The Yi Ji Company was founded in Shanghai by prominent figures Tao Xingru, Li Xiehe, Wen Qinpu, and others. Wheat Boat Sunk by Coal Ship 154

Xi Bocheng, a merchant of miscellaneous grains from Huaiyang, hired Yang Linggui's Chaohu boat to transport 400 bags of wheat to Shanghai for sale. The ship was sailing outside the mouth of Liuhe a few days ago when it was suddenly overtaken by a coal ship of an unknown nationality at full speed. Yang's boat could not avoid it and was rammed and sunk. More than a dozen people on board fell into the water. Fortunately, they were rescued by fishing boats, and Yang and eight crew members were saved. The rest are presumed to have drowned. Yesterday, Yang and the rescued crew members reported to the merchants in Shanghai. It is said that the wheat and the boat were worth more than 5,000 yuan. The name of the ship is being investigated in order to negotiate compensation for the loss of the ship and cargo.

Waste Burning at Wusong Huafeng Factory Triggers Explosion of Garbage Shell 155

A "Seven-Born" Fifth-Class Huang Bomb

A Loud Explosion Creates a Large Ground Hole

The Huafeng Yarn Factory on the west end of Wusong Yuncao Creek has been undergoing internal repairs and cleaning recently. Yesterday (the 5th) at 10:30 AM, a worker was burning garbage in the open space behind the factory when, unexpectedly, a "seven-born" fifth-class shell was mixed in with the garbage. It detonated instantly, causing a loud explosion and black smoke to fill the sky. Shell fragments scattered everywhere, creating a large hole in the ground. Fortunately, no one was nearby, so no casualties occurred. Patrol Officer Tong Boya of the 1st Precinct of the 7th District heard about it and immediately took Patrol Officer Zhou Heshan to the scene for inspection. They also recovered a damaged shell casing. The patrol officer, because the factory is operated by Japanese merchants, and the Sino-Japanese dispute has not yet subsided, feared that there might be other reasons and that they might make excuses. Therefore, he had to find out the truth. After investigating everywhere and confirming that there were no other circumstances, he only took the damaged shell casing back to the station to report.

Water Outage at Longji Lane Resolved 156

The Shanghai Real Estate Association has received a reply from the Municipal Council regarding the water supply to Longji Lane, North Zhejiang Road, which was cut off by the water company, causing a dispute. The matter has been resolved. The letters are recorded as follows: (1) Shanghai Real Estate Association to the General Office of the Public Concession Municipal Council, (November 4, 21st year): Sir, with reference to your office's response No. 1408 on October 27th, stating that the water source in Longji Lane has been restored, and enclosing a copy of the Shanghai Waterworks Co.'s reply, we have read it with respect. This kind of event, which could easily cause a major dispute, has been peacefully corrected, which is truly commendable and intelligent behavior on the part of the water company. The association anticipates that if a solution is sought from the perspective of both law and fact, a satisfactory resolution will be achieved. However, with regard to your office's inquiry to the association, asking whether it is fair and reasonable to continue not paying the arrears, the association can frankly answer that if the arrears arise from a dispute between the two parties, it is absolutely not fair and reasonable. Your office, we trust, will agree. Furthermore, regarding whether the water company's actions are oppressive to the association, after reading the draft letter from Longzhang Co. to the water company, we can draw a conclusion. (2) Public Concession Municipal Council replying to the Shanghai Real Estate Association, (October 28th): We acknowledge your major letter of October 25th, protesting the water outage in Longji Lane. Upon receiving the information, this bureau immediately inquired with the Shanghai Waterworks Co. Now, we present the reasons given by the company for your perusal. After reviewing them, we would like to ask whether you still consider the company's actions to be oppressive. Before the meter system was implemented, the houses in that area owed a total of 1,503.31 yuan in water fees from April to September. This issue has now been resolved. However, since your association has protested, we ask whether you consider it fair and reasonable to continue not paying the arrears. We hereby reply in this regard for your information. (3) Waterworks Co. to the Municipal Council, in response to your telephone inquiry to our general manager regarding the water supply at 716 and 717 North Zhejiang Road: The houses there are the property of Longzhang Co. The details of this incident are as follows: (1) On November 18th of last year, it was discovered that there was a rubber hose at 743 and 745 North Zhejiang Road, Yuda Dyeing Factory, connected to the water at 738 for dyeing purposes. According to the tenant of the house, it was one of the owners of the dyeing factory. (2) On the 23rd of the same month, our company informed Longzhang Co. of this matter and stated that in order to prevent water theft, the houses there would be charged according to water meter rates. (3) After sending the letter, there was no response. On January 6th of this year, another letter was sent, but because the landlord did not take any action, the water supply was cut off. As a result, a water meter contract was signed on the 15th. (4) For various reasons, the water meter readings totaled 1,503.31 yuan. (5) After March of this year, the dyeing factory's water fees gradually increased to twice the previous amount, proving that there was indeed water theft before. (6) The landlord refused to pay the fees. Our company issued a notice on October 13th and informed the tenants. The landlord, in addition to requesting that fees be charged according to the old system, had no other way to satisfy our company. Therefore, the water supply was cut off on the 24th. (7) The entire area where the houses are located began to install water meters on October 1st. (8) A representative from this company came to agree to discount the water fees for the entire period, which would resolve the matter immediately. This was because the landlord had difficulty preventing water theft. However, if the landlord had taken action promptly after receiving our company's notice last December, it would have satisfied the dyeing factory. (9) After the matter was resolved, the water supply was immediately restored. We hope that you will investigate this matter.

Autopsy Conducted on Woman Killed by Fire Engine 160

Fire Department of the Northern District Appropriates Compensation

Yesterday's report stated that a fire engine in the Northern District of the Southern City ran over and killed Hu Shi when it passed in front of the Bulangxin Medicine Shop on Fangbang Road. It has now been learned that the 9th Pujiadi (local leader) Jiang Pingyang was ordered by the police station to report the incident to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Wu and other medical examiners were dispatched to the scene and found that Hu Shi's death was caused by a head injury. The local leader was ordered to find the family of the deceased and provide a coffin. Yesterday evening, her husband Hu Zhongkang heard the news and arrived at the scene, grieving over the body. The police took Hu to the police station, where he stated that he was 25 years old, from Haimen, and currently residing at 437 Guangfu Temple Street, working as a peddler. The deceased was his wife, Hu Shi, also 25 years old, with two sons and one daughter. The eldest son is seven years old, the second son is five years old, and the daughter is four years old. His wife had been living in their hometown of Haimen and had just arrived in Shanghai from their hometown less than ten days ago. Now she has died tragically, and he requests justice. Yesterday, it was ordered that the driver, A Gao, who caused the accident, be sent to the Third Division of the Public Security Bureau for questioning. Meanwhile, the father of the deceased, Shi Shunqing, went to the Northern District Fire Department to request compensation. The director of the district, Lu Jinlin, contacted him and, considering that the family was very poor, agreed to provide 100 yuan in addition to the coffin and clothing. The body has already been placed in a coffin. In addition to the deceased, two pedestrians were also injured. One was Chen Degui, 52 years old, from Shanbei, the owner of the Chen Defeng Candle Shop south of the Shui Xian Temple, who suffered injuries to his kidneys and right knee. The other was Yang Yonghua, 57 years old, from Changzhou, who had been a teacher in his hometown and had come to Shanghai for business. He was residing at 44 North Xizang Road at the home of his nephew, the owner of the Shunxing Palm Mattress Shop. He suffered injuries to his forehead, right hand, left foot, and buttocks. His injuries were less severe than Chen's. Both injured men are currently being treated at the Shanghai Hospital.

Robberies in Jiangwan and Pudong 161

At one hour and one moment this morning, bandits broke into the home of Guo Rui, near Niulang Temple on West Street in the jurisdiction of the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District of Jiangwan. Six bandits wearing short clothes, all speaking in the Jiangbei dialect, and armed with firearms, broke into the house, showed their guns, and forbade anyone from making a sound. They robbed more than ten yuan in cash, cotton quilts, mosquito nets, and other items. After the robbery, the bandits fled west with their loot. Patrol police officers from the jurisdiction arrested two bandits, Zhang Jing and Chai Jinqing, near Guo's home and took them to the station for questioning before sending them to the Third Division of the General Bureau for legal action.

Also, it was reported that at 7:00 PM this afternoon, Dong Jinfu's house in Tangjiazhai, Luxing District, Pudong, was robbed of more than forty yuan in cash, and the robbers escaped without a trace.

Special Item

Report on the Situation of the Shanghai Public Concession by Judge Fessenden, Volume 4 (15) 168

14. When the powers of the municipal government are strictly limited by law, the authority to order compensation for misused public funds is particularly important. Moreover, the central government also believes that using the method of auditing accounts to ensure that the municipal government complies with these restrictions is appropriate and effective. However, as far as auditing the accounts of the Shanghai Municipal Council is concerned, under the current situation, it does not seem necessary to grant the auditor the power to impose penalties and compensation. Furthermore, implementing this new law may cause difficulties and objections with the council. Therefore, whether it is appropriate is a question. My opinion is that if the auditor discovers any incidents involving the legal responsibility of any council member during the audit, the Board of Directors can exercise its discretion to handle the matter and file civil or criminal lawsuits against one or more of the related parties.

15. Therefore, to enable the auditor of the Municipal Council's accounts to perform their duties, I believe it is only necessary to allow them to freely inspect the Municipal Council's books and registers. At the same time, it should be clearly stipulated in the Council's rules that all Council employees should provide the auditor with all books, accounts, vouchers, and related documents and records for verification when needed.

D. Format of the Auditor's Report or Certificate

16. According to current practice, the auditor of the Municipal Council's accounts should sign a certificate in the following format at the end of the list of expenditures in the Municipal Council's accounts for the year published in the annual report: (The above accounts have been audited by the auditor together with the books and vouchers, and it is hereby certified that, according to the books and vouchers, the above accounts are free of errors.)

17. In some countries, there is another practice, namely that the auditor auditing the municipal government's accounts should sign a more detailed certificate, explaining various points that may or may not be considered included in the above ordinary certificate.

18. For example, the current municipal regulations of Durban stipulate that the auditor should annually certify the following matters:

(1) Whether the accounts of the Municipal Council are accurate;

(2) If there are any business ventures, whether all accounts are recorded separately;

(3) Whether the published accounts accurately reflect the financial position of the Municipal Council, the various matters it handles, and the results of its business (if any);

(4) Whether adequate preparations have been made to repay any funds borrowed by the Municipal Council, such as municipal bonds, promissory notes, or others;

(5) Whether the funds allocated to compensate for the depreciation and obsolescence of mechanical equipment are sufficient;

(6) Whether the value of municipally owned property is fair;

(7) Whether all the auditor's needs have been met, and whether their suggestions have been implemented.

19. I believe that it is beneficial for the certificate issued by the auditor to clearly include the above points. However, the wording of the above clauses should be revised, as some of them are more applicable to commercial businesses and not very applicable to public institutions. For example, regarding item (3), it has been pointed out to me that the municipal government's (financial position) ultimately depends on various factors not recorded in the accounts, such as the population in the city area and the assessed value of land and houses from which taxes can be collected. If this clause is amended to (the financial position as reflected in the Municipal Council's records), the wording would be more appropriate. Also, regarding item (6), it has been pointed out that it is extremely difficult for the auditor to issue a certificate proving (whether the value of all municipally owned property is fair). This is because most of the municipal government's property cannot be sold to obtain its value, such as bridges, sewers, and land acquired for road construction. These types of properties are listed under the (development account) in the Public Concession's statement of revenue and expenditure. Therefore, the auditor's certificate should specify the basis of valuation used, namely its cost. This wording would be more appropriate.

20. In addition, there is another point that could be suggested for inclusion in the certificate, namely that the auditor should specifically address the issue of tax collection and express experiences gained elsewhere. Laxity in tax collection is one of the most common causes of difficulties in municipal government accounts. Laxity gives rise to various malpractices, causing certain classes of people who are legally liable to pay taxes to evade property taxes or other municipal taxes, or failing to accurately estimate rents, so that all property taxes, whether levied based on the cost of the property or according to its rentable value, have accurate and uniform standards. Furthermore, in this regard, a clause could be added to the auditor's certificate, requiring the auditor to certify (whether all revenue obtainable from taxes has been calculated according to the regulations and with proper standards, and whether it has been appropriately recorded in the accounts).

21. As for the final clause, item (7), regarding the auditor's needs and recommendations, including it in the certificate may disclose matters that the auditor recommends should be kept confidential for the public interest. Therefore, in addition to issuing a certificate for publication, the auditor should be required to submit a report to the Finance Committee, so that they can freely and confidentially raise issues regarding the Municipal Council's registration of accounts or other financial management matters for the committee's consideration, without including the final clause in the published certificate. It seems that auditors of public institutions in the United Kingdom have adopted this approach.

22. I now propose that the format of the Durban auditor's certificate mentioned above be adopted after being modified as proposed above.

(Note 1) See Chapter 6 of Part 5 of this report.

(Note 2) See Section 43 of Chapter 6 of Part 5 of this report.

(Note 3) See Section 60 of Chapter 6 of Part 5 of this report.

(Note 4) See (1) and (10) of Section 6 of Chapter 6 of Part 5 of this report.

(Note 5) Regarding this point, see Section 20 and Sections 26-27 of Chapter 5 of Part 4 of this report.

(Note 6) The principle that government auditors should enjoy reasonable tenure protection is a well-recognized principle. The Durban Municipal Regulations have set a precedent for extending this principle to municipal government auditors. (To be continued)

Random Notes

Eulogy 169

— Zhan Lu

Social customs regarding weddings and funerals differ between the past and the present. The extravagance of weddings is gradually being reduced and simplified. However, the extravagance of funerals has not only not decreased compared to the past, but has also become more extreme, increasingly hypocritical and extravagant! Therefore, grand weddings are becoming less common, while grand funerals, using the deceased to show off, are becoming more and more frequent.

Since the political reform, everything has been transitioning from aristocratic to democratic. However, when it comes to funerals, things revert from democratic to aristocratic. As long as one is willing to spend money, even if it's a cat or a dog that has died, the funeral can be arranged with the pomp of high officials and nobles, complete with road signs, heralds, Western and Chinese music, grand retinues, and even the ceremonial guards from the City God Temple can be added. Gaining the praise of onlookers for the grand spectacle is considered the height of glory.

If it were just the grand funeral itself, that would be one thing. But those families who treat funerals as a performance also send out special obituaries, the thicker the better. I once saw an obituary printed for the death of an old foreman at a printing shop, which was two inches thick. The delivery men complained endlessly, blaming the printing shop owner for adding to the thickness. The shop spared no expense on its own products, but didn't consider that the couriers carrying the obituaries were almost crushed under the weight.

Inside the obituaries are stacks upon stacks of eulogies. When a village elder dies in the countryside, at least the village head and district chief are asked to write eulogies. When an old foreman of a grocery store dies in the city, at least the Minister of Industry and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce are asked. These can still be considered appropriate to their status. Even more absurd are the forged eulogies from important figures, with phrases like "His merits will remain in the Republic" and "Kind heart and chivalrous spirit" printed on them, completely unrelated to the subject. Recently, when the father of a lawyer who specializes in soliciting lawsuits died, he reprinted eulogies from other people's obituaries, prominently displaying the names of central government officials on the obituary, which led to the official investigation and the humorous situation of seeking honor but finding shame.

Obituaries are inherently deceptive, with phrases like "weeping blood" and "in a daze from grief" already telling a great lie. Adding all kinds of inappropriate eulogies on top of that is like deception within deception, a great lie made even greater! Alas!

The Driving Force Behind Shanghai's Prosperity 170

— Jin Butong

｜(Prostitution) (Gambling) (Opium)｜

How Shanghai has become so prosperous is a question worthy of study.

Some say that Shanghai's prosperity is due to its strategic location at the gateway to the Yangtze River, with convenient water and land transportation, attracting merchants from all directions. Some say that Shanghai's early opening to foreign trade and the arrival of foreigners, who landed in Shanghai and gradually mixed with people from all over, led to its prosperity. Others say that Shanghai is the financial center of the country, and its economic power has driven its prosperity.

On the surface, these reasons seem sufficient. However, a closer look at Shanghai's society reveals that the true driving force behind its prosperity is not these factors.

The primary driving force behind Shanghai's prosperity is (prostitution). Because of (prostitution), the catering and clothing industries have flourished day by day. When the Public Concession banned prostitution in the past, the market plummeted. As the "nightingales" moved south, the market in the French Concession gradually prospered. This is powerful proof.

The second driving force is (gambling). From roulette games with tens of thousands of silver taels at stake to flower games with a copper coin as the prize, all kinds of gambling are available. Those who lose gamble away their houses, lands, and even their wives and children. Smaller losses inevitably lead to pawning. This directly and indirectly supports the livelihoods of many people in Shanghai.

The third driving force is (opium). It directly benefits the owners and staff of opium dens, not to mention the indirect contribution to Shanghai's night market. The golden age of the French Concession saw opium dens lined up east of Eight Immortals Bridge, and the business of fruit stores and restaurants could be lively until dawn. This shows the greatness of its influence.

The market in the Chinese-controlled areas has never been prosperous because (prostitution), (gambling), and (opium) are prohibited. The market in the concessions is so good because (prostitution), (gambling), and (opium) are not prohibited. This is the fundamental reason for Shanghai's prosperity. It is said that the Japanese are promoting (prostitution), (gambling), and (opium) in the Northeast, which is quite logical.

The Idol of Science 171

— Hen

｜Originally a Deception｜

This is a news story about a comical, laughable, and scientific deception that occurred in Guangxi about two months ago. I can guarantee that this is not a fabricated story, as a friend who just came here from Guangxi told me about it.

Superstition in divine power is one of the most pathetic and despicable shortcomings of our Chinese people. Even in Shanghai, which is known as the most civilized city in Southeast Asia, there is still the Rainbow Temple and Wu Jianguang on Nanjing Road, which represents Shanghai. Not to mention the interior of Guangxi, which has not been baptized by 20th-century civilization. If we randomly ask a young villager there, "Who is the current Chairman of the National Government?" he will stare blankly and not know the answer. But if we ask him about the era and deeds of Guan Yu, he will answer fluently as if reciting family treasures. In every village, there are many temples. (God, give me happiness!) Every first and fifteenth day of the lunar month, one can see many pious men and women praying in any temple. Clever swindlers took advantage of this to perform their comical deception.

"Isn't this a true god descending? There is a statue of a god in a certain temple that can stand in the center of a box without ropes or anything else tying it." After this news spread, villagers from all villages came to this temple to worship. Sure enough, the rumors were true. Through a small hole in a sealed wooden box, one could see a statue of a god suspended in the center, indeed without anything tying it. The temple keeper (the one who looks after the temple) said, "This god has descended in person to investigate because there are many wicked people here. Everyone must sincerely pay respects to it." As a result, a lot of incense money flowed into the temple keeper's pocket.

Secrets cannot be kept from people forever. This strange thing was discovered by the local government, who sent someone to investigate. The trick was exposed. It turned out that the statue of the god was made of iron, and the surrounding of the box contained the same magnetic material. The suction force from all sides and above and below was equal, so the iron statue of the god was sucked in the middle. After the matter was clarified, this scientific god came to an end.

Menstrual Gleanings 172

— Qi Huai

In old China, menstruation was called "tian gui" (heavenly gui). German farmers, however, call it the "rose crown."

Among savage races, women during menstruation are often confined. Among African natives, the place where women during menstruation reside must be marked with a red flag for identification.

The amount of menstrual blood each time ranges from about two fluid ounces to four fluid ounces, up to eight fluid ounces.

In countries around the world, the average age of women's first menstruation is 14.1 years in the United States. The earliest is in France, at 12.6 years, and the latest is in Russia and Switzerland, at 19 years. The earliest age for Japanese women is nine years and seven months, and the latest is twenty-one years and ten months. The average age in China is 17 years.

Menstruation occurs on average every 28 days, with a minimum of two weeks and a maximum of six weeks.

The most common duration of each menstruation is about three days. Followed by four to five days, five days, seven days, and four days.

According to old Chinese sayings, menstruation ceases at seven sevens, which is forty-nine years old: but according to Senisi's statistics, the average age is 47.1 years.

In addition to blood, menstrual blood also contains mucus, broken cells, bacteria, and granular debris.

A characteristic of menstrual blood is that it does not easily coagulate: even after a long time, it still maintains its inherent liquid state.

Menstruation is often seen as mysterious. According to Eckath's description, in Italy, menstrual cloths from a virgin's first menstruation are sold as amulets to ward off disease.

Mantello recorded that a child menstruated at the age of three and gave birth to a child at the age of six.

News Briefs Gu Tai-furen, the mother of Cai Diaotu, owner of the Guangming Theater and the Anlong newspaper, celebrated her sixtieth birthday on the sixth of this month. Mr. Diaotu specially prepared a longevity feast to celebrate his mother's birthday. Famous opera performers from Shanghai performed Peking opera at the Cai residence on that day. The performances numbered more than twenty. Gao Huizhu, the adopted granddaughter of Tai-furen, is a famous movie star. She also sang Peking opera and performed a play with Diaotu to honor her elders. It is also said that the birthday celebration was held at the main residence in Chenjiaxing Town, Sanlintang, Pudong. There were two reception areas, one at No. 8 Pu Bai Fang, Luban Road, Beishi, and one at Guanqiao, Nanshi. Pu Bai Fang had many cars available, while the Minnan Wheel Company at Guanqiao had special ships available to transport guests. It was very convenient for guests to go to the Cai residence. The special ship was scheduled to depart three times in the morning at 8:00, 10:00, and 12:00, and once in the afternoon at 2:00. It only takes one hour to reach the Cai residence, it is said.

The Crossroads of Death 173

— Fan Yanqiao

But I don't know what the reason was? Muliang felt lost and absent-minded that night. He was too lazy to read the tabloids and too lazy to read novels. He smoked cigarettes particularly hurriedly, finishing a cigarette in less than half the usual time, throwing it into the spittoon with a "hiss" sound. In less than three minutes, the sound was heard again. As usual, after dinner, Aigu came to the bedroom to tidy up and arrange the things needed for the night. She was very busy walking back and forth. She also felt that the young master was different from usual. Wherever she went, two sharp eyes followed her relentlessly, especially when she got close to him. She could see him looking at her intensely, with an awkward smile.

While Lawyer Xia and Muliang were having a secret conversation in the study that had lasted for three hours without ending, Old Wang, the gatekeeper, came and whispered a few words in Muliang's ear. Muliang waved his hand and said, "Tell him to go to Lawyer Xia's residence tomorrow to talk." Old Wang agreed with a "yes" and went out to tell Liu Da, who had come from a remote village. Liu Da agreed and left. Then an irregular discussion meeting started in the gatehouse. Xiao San, the rickshaw puller, said first, "A young adopted daughter-in-law is worth at most two hundred yuan." Ah Liu, the deputy gatekeeper, said, "It's not like the villagers trading with each other in the countryside. Naturally, this amount is considered high. Now that villagers are trading with city people, why not make some good deals?" Lao Wu said resentfully, "The world is becoming less and less like the world. I'm afraid that in the future, all villagers will have no descendants." Xiao San said, "Old Uncle is wrong. With money, it's easy to find a wife, even two or three." Old Wang took a few big puffs of the remaining yellow tobacco from the pipe. In the very light smoke, he said, "Even if they agree to the request, two hundred yuan, five or six years of hard work, food and clothing, is more than just this amount! Maybe you can't even get that much in hand." Just as he was about to express some moral arguments, the master had already sent Lawyer Xia out, so they had to end the discussion without a conclusion.

The next day, Lawyer Xia came again and solemnly handed Muliang a red card that was a bit worn. Muliang took it and brought out one hundred and fifty yuan from inside and handed it to Lawyer Xia. From then on, Aigu's (jurisdiction) was transferred.

A week later, Muliang held a banquet and invited relatives and friends to have a celebratory drink. Everyone congratulated him on his good fortune in getting a beautiful concubine. But the first wife was so angry that she didn't eat for a day, deeply regretting that she had put in so much effort before to change her to adapt to the times and made it easy for her husband.

As for Aigu, she was probably smug, right?

Gold Prices Fell Last Week 174

｜Reversal After Three Weeks of Continuous Rise｜

Last week, the gold market's telegraphic prices fluctuated. Although the daily fluctuations were moderate, unlike the previous violent ups and downs, the news of the national team's selling off caused people to lose hope. Initially, due to the near-rise in silver prices and the fall in American cotton, the market opened high, with the December price at 753.8 taels, an increase of 1.4 taels. Later, as exchange rates turned favorable and spot demand rose, the market became active, and the central bank's absorption of spot goods caused the price to reach 759.1 taels in the afternoon. The next day, the exchange rate rose, and the market saw a sudden reversal, falling sharply by more than 10 taels, breaking through the 50-tael mark. After the silver market and exchange rate rose, the price reached 43 taels. Later, as American companies settled their accounts, the price fluctuated, although the domestic market was long. Because there was news that the United Kingdom was considering restoring the gold standard after suspending it, opponents were very strong, causing gold prices to trend downward. Until Thursday, when there was news that 21 banks of various sizes in the United States had collapsed, gold prices immediately rebounded back above the 50-tael mark. Unexpectedly, Hengxing continued to sell aggressively. There was also a Reuters report that the US Treasury's silver reserves were insufficient, causing negative news such as the plan to purchase raw silver to spread. The market was filled with pessimism, and the price finally fell to 43.2 taels. Later, as the silver market was stable and the Shanghai exchange rate was also stable, Hengxing continued to sell relentlessly, preventing the market price from rising. Fortunately, the US exchange rate was still strong, which stabilized the market. Until Saturday, when the European exchange rate seemed firm, the British exchange rate continued to rise, and the US exchange rate remained unchanged, but the overnight bearish view was not fulfilled, and the forward price rebounded. The market's sentiment softened, and gold prices fell slightly. Hengxing and Yifeng continued to sell non-stop, with the price suddenly dropping to a low of 742 taels in the morning. At the close, the price was 44.9 taels. Comparing with the previous Saturday, the price fell by 7.5 taels, a reversal after three weeks of continuous rise of 26.9 taels. The difference between the highest and lowest prices for the entire week was 17.1 taels (the difference between the opening and closing prices was 8.9 taels). It is said that Hengxing alone sold about 13,000 to 14,000 bars this week. It is estimated that the profit is over 10 taels per bar. The various firms, such as Dalian Gang, Qianchangxiang, Hengyu, Fuchang, Yuanheng, Tianfengyong, etc., were all long. The short firms include Tongtaichang, Yuanmaoyong, Yifeng, and Ruikang. As for the overseas silver market, the British silver price continued to rise, and the US silver price rebounded. The local exchange market went in the opposite direction. The listed British gold price fell by half a point (125), and the US gold price was flat. The exchange rate turned high, so the British side was tight and the American side was loose. The exchange rate was initially around 60 taels, and later it was 70 taels. It is estimated that the exchange rate of British to American rose by 1.125 points, and the US to British rebounded by 1.375 points, a rebound after falling for seven weeks. The trend this week is expected to be a consolidation. The high and low prices of the British and American silver markets and the gold market are listed below:
